<div id="review_393810007" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393810007" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393810007?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6972914-karen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393810007" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6738406207514563409"><b>5 BRILLIANT ACTION-PACKED STARS!!!!!!</b><br/>I LOVED THIS BOOK EVEN MORE THAN THE FIRST!!!!! (if that is even possible). <br/>I LOVE THESE BOYS!!!!!!!!<br/><br/>Sticks and Stones basically begins about 5 months after the conclusion of their first case together. Ty and Zane had been apart during this time on separate assignments.. and recovering from their ordeal with the Tri-State murders. Both guys have been suffering mentally, not only from a bit of PTSD, but also from their separation. It is apparent to both men th</span>
  <span id="freeText6738406207514563409" style="display:none"><b>5 BRILLIANT ACTION-PACKED STARS!!!!!!</b><br>I LOVED THIS BOOK EVEN MORE THAN THE FIRST!!!!! (if that is even possible). <br>I LOVE THESE BOYS!!!!!!!!<br><br>Sticks and Stones basically begins about 5 months after the conclusion of their first case together. Ty and Zane had been apart during this time on separate assignments.. and recovering from their ordeal with the Tri-State murders. Both guys have been suffering mentally, not only from a bit of PTSD, but also from their separation. It is apparent to both men that they are developing feelings for the other, but neither is willing or able to share this information with the other. Whether it be for the obvious reasons of their FBI partnership, or out of fear of rejection...neither one is anywhere near sharing.<br><br>Zane in particular is suffering. He is repeatedly failing his mental evals for the bureau, and is being threatened with early retirement if he can't get himself together soon. He has been forced into therapy, and is not having much success. And it's not helping that he has been pining for the company of a partner that he's not even sure wants to work with him anymore. He had tried to contact Ty over the 5 months of their separation, but was unable to reach him.<br><br>Ty on the other hand, was doing his best to cope. Working covert side jobs for his boss, Richard Burns, and sleeping around to try to drive Zane from his thoughts, Ty had almost convinced himself that he was coping. But his well-known craziness has even taken on new levels of bravado. So much so, that he has started taking too many chances, and has started to worry his boss. He is usually much better at covering-up his inner struggles, but lately, not so much. <br><br>Brought back together after 5 months apart, the two fall right back into their fail-safe mode of coping, with the verbal sparing and evasive nature of communicating. It is clear that they still feel the pull and the mutual attraction, but they are both apprehensive about sharing feelings. They are both obviously suffering, and now begin to realize that their struggles have become apparent to their boss.<br><br>So Richard Burns places them both on mandatory vacation for 2-3 weeks, and has withheld their evals for their return, in order to try to salvage Zane's career, and Ty's mental status. He has also ordered Ty to return home to visit his family in West Virginia. And he has strongly suggested that Zane get some therapy in order to pass his mental eval.<br><br>Ty then decides to ask Zane to join him on his trip home. Zane does accept the invitation but not without misgivings. And here is where the story takes off. Once in West Virginia, the two decide to go on a prolonged hiking trip through the Appalachian Trail with Ty's overbearing father Earl, and his Psychiatrist brother, Deacon. The Grady boys do know the mountains well, but none of them are prepared for the adventure that they encounter on their trip.<br><br>And let me tell you, the interactions with Ty's family at the farm are absolutely priceless. And his Grandfather, with that shovel....HILARIOUS!!!<br><br>Ty struggles with his feelings for Zane, and also fights his insecurities where his father is concerned. Meanwhile, Deacon "Deuce," tries to psychoanalyze Zane and his mental struggles and fears along the way. Well eventually the trip starts to go south... and bad things start happening... and happening.... and happening. Things really get intense, people might die, and Zane and Ty are suddenly struggling to keep them all alive. It is a riveting story. Often intense, sometimes funny, but NEVER a dull moment!! <br><br><b>
  <i>"Sounds like lions and tigers and bears, oh my," Zane said..</i>
</b><br><br>But through their struggles, Ty and Zane are forced to face their feelings for each other, and both, while silent, realize their unspoken need for the other. So many great lines, and tender moments, this book was a masterpiece!! The author has completely hooked me on these two guys!!! <br><br><b>
  <i>You listen to me, Beaumont Tyler Grady. You are a wise-cracking, stubborn, annoying pain in the ass who lives to cause trouble. You're also a brave courageous, and valiant Marine who puts his life on the line for what he believes and for those he loves. There is no way you have ever been or will be a coward. It simply isn't you."</i>
</b><br><br>From the "Butch and Sundance scene at Quantico, to the literal "DELIVERANCE" from the mountain, I was loving every moment. Such great witty writing, and so intense at times, I felt like I was up their on the mountain with them....heart racing, cold and wet at times, I felt like I lived it right along with them. <br><br><b>
  <i>"You're okay," Zane said quietly but clearly. "Just focus on me for a few minutes. What's the first thing that comes to mind?" While talking he was gently wiping away the blood.<br>Ty blinked at him, opening his mouth as he thought the very first thing that came to mind when Zane prompted him. </i>
</b>I love you.<b> He snapped his mouth closed and stared at Zane, unable and unwilling to answer.</b><br><br>But honestly, what really has me hooked is the strong bond these guys are forming. I absolutely love their relationship. <br><br><b>
  <i>What he was afraid of, he'd come to realize, was not dark spaces or falling from great heights or being buried alive. His greatest fears, in the end, were letting down those he loved and saying the words "I love you" without any hope of hearing them in return.</i>
</b><br><br>And I can't wait to see where they go from here. I cannot recommend these books enough. Excellent writing!!! LOVE LOVE LOVE!!!!<br><br>No less than <b>5 STARS</b><br><br>My pics...<br><br><b>Ty Grady</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men/ChanningTatum2.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380909321i/3179407.jpg" alt="Channing Tatum photo ChanningTatum2.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Zane Garrett</b><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men/MarcoDapper84-1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380909321i/3179408._SY540_.jpg" alt="Marco Dapper photo MarcoDapper84-1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="6738406207514563409" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText9469333906676891565" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Awesome Ty &amp; Zane Stars!!!</b><br><br>  Ty and Zane are back!   <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379794954i/598949.jpg" alt=" photo 8dca51bd-a968-4a98-9578-4293dba404e0_zps5ab641cb.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“And FYI, Deliverance took place in Georgia. In West Virginia we kiss our cousins.” -Ty</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/130140e8-de47-44c7-a5e4-53f5ae86da08_zps10507a5c.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Hell would be more relaxing that this. And I could get a tan.” -Zane</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I LOVE TY AND ZANE! Okay, now that that’s out of the way... lets get to the story! (A short summary)  <br><br>Ty and Zane are at Ty’s home. Everything is good so far. His family thinks Zane is only Ty’s work partner (except his brother, who knows), but they all treat Zane like he is one of theirs and they really are a crazy and funny family! Ty and Zane go on a hike throughout the mountains with Ty’s dad and brother Deuce (who I adored!). Everything is all good, until they run into some REAL crazies- then the action happens!!!! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Treasure hunters, guns, bombs, grenades, cougars attacking... these boys go through the ringer!!! It’s really a miracle they make it out alive! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>This is the WORST vacation ever! <br><br><br>I loved the ending... although I really wanted them to just COME OUT AND SAY IT!!! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The ‘I love you’... I know it is hard for both of them to admit. Maybe the next one they will be able to admit those feelings to each other. But really, those 3 little words... I thought for sure when Ty was about to go into septic shock he would FINALLY say it, but no!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/52e69482-4a50-46c8-bafc-7dd140db804f_zps2930b729.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409692i/802363.jpg" alt=" photo 52e69482-4a50-46c8-bafc-7dd140db804f_zps2930b729.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What they did convey/say to each other was beautiful though...<br><br> Zane had his moments-<br><b>
  <blockquote>He couldn’t tear his eyes away from Ty, even knowing Deuce was watching, and Zane knew right then and there that he wouldn’t be giving Ty up without a fight. Ever.<br><br><i>“You listen to me, Beaumont Tyler Grady. You are a wise-cracking, stubborn, annoying pain in the ass who lives to cause trouble. You’re also a brave, courageous, and valiant Marine who puts his life on the line for what he believes and for those he loves. There is no way you have ever been or ever will be a coward. It simply isn’t in you.” </i>
</blockquote>
</b><br>As did Ty-<br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/54fca8a3-db66-4491-b412-0fd40263d08e_zps50c216df.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380409692i/802364.jpg" alt=" photo 54fca8a3-db66-4491-b412-0fd40263d08e_zps50c216df.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I loved watching their relationship grow and evolve! Even though they didn’t admit all of their feelings to each other, they admitted them to themselves, and thats a huge step for these two guys. I’m really looking forward to learning more about both men and watching them grow as the series continues. <br>Both guys were really yummy, per usual, and even though Ty is my man, I found myself loving Zane much more in this book... Perhaps it’s because he would do anything to protect Ty. Can’t wait to get further into this series! Love it!<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Sticks and stones may break my bones, but words will never hurt me.</blockquote>

<div id="review_221322177" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/221322177" />
    <a title="Baba  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669232-baba"><img alt="Baba  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564910043p2/4669232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/221322177?book_show_action=true">Oct 10, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Baba  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Baba  " href="/user/show/4669232-baba">Baba  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669232-baba?shelf=m-m">m-m</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4669232-baba?shelf=books-kelly-and-baba-liked-or-loved">books-kelly-and-baba-liked-or-loved</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer221322177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13724379853293338779">“Sticks and stones may break my bones, but words will never hurt me.”<br/><br/>3.5 stars.<br/><br/>I rounded up to four stars because Ty and Zane are just great! Again, loved all those witty dialogs and I really liked Ty’s brother Deacon (Deuce)! However, I had a huge problem with Ty’s father, Earl. He is such a stupid jerk! And I had issues with the plot. When I was 46 % done with Sticks & Stones I got rather annoyed. In fact, Ty’s father was causing a substantial clusterfuck. He insulted his son in a way that I f</span>
  <span id="freeText13724379853293338779" style="display:none">“Sticks and stones may break my bones, but words will never hurt me.”<br /><br />3.5 stars.<br /><br />I rounded up to four stars because Ty and Zane are just great! Again, loved all those witty dialogs and I really liked Ty’s brother Deacon (Deuce)! However, I had a huge problem with Ty’s father, Earl. He is such a stupid jerk! And I had issues with the plot. When I was 46 % done with Sticks &amp; Stones I got rather annoyed. In fact, Ty’s father was causing a substantial clusterfuck. He insulted his son in a way that I found totally disrespectful! I got all worked up because what happened afterwards...jeez, so stupid! The author used this situation to induce a bit of suspense. I was so not happy with the plot at that time.<br /><br />I’m going to switch to a brief synopsis.<br /><br />The book starts out with a merry FBI training session. I did enjoy this start! Later, Ty and Zane are seeing Assistant Director Burns and he says “Garrett is going on a little vacation...” Yes, and Ty is on leave, too. Burns is not so pleased about their psych evaluations and therefore both of them have to relax a bit more and are expected to pass the next evaluations with flying colors. Ty decides to go home and see his family. Naturally, Zane comes along...<br /><br />It was fun to read about Ty’s family and their banter. I can relate to this hiking tour as well, but that’s as far as it goes because what happened there...tsk, tsk, tsk. They had to deal with a few bad guys, rain and cold, and dangerous animals.<br /><br />I liked the first 45 % of this book and then the shit hit the fan. I got all worked up about the next 15 % of Sticks &amp; Stones. And this whole fallout Ty had to deal with...not nice. I could have smacked his dad. All his fault – ok, the author’s fault. Gosh, I was so angry! Anyway, I have to say that it was interesting to see how Ty and his dad had to sort out their issues. And it’s yet more interesting to see how their 'relationship' is developing. It grows slowly but steadily. I enjoyed to read about their thoughts and how protective they are about each other.<br /><br />Memorable “quotes”:<br /><br />[...]“Are you still pissy about the rubber band cannon?” Ty asked him in exasperation.<br />“Ugh.” Zane started unbuttoning the BDU blouse. “You’re lucky that guy from accounting didn’t know it was you when his toupee went flying. He might have rerouted your next paycheck to Greenpeace.”[...]<br /><br />Zane to Ty’s father:<br />[...]”You owe him a hell of a lot more than just pretty words.” Zane paused, his banked anger melting into a quiet, pained sadness. “I don’t know what you thought you were doing, but you couldn’t have said anything that would have hurt him more.”[...]<br /><br />[...]What he was afraid of, he’d come to realize, was not dark spaces or falling from great heights or being buried alive. His greatest fears, in the end, were letting down those he loved and saying the words “I love you” without any hope of hearing them in return. He knew, deep down somewhere, that if he fell for Zane Garrett, he’d be falling alone.[...]<br /><br /><br />I’m going to cut and run because I need a little break. I’ll be back for sure, though and I’m going to read book 3 and 4.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16009064115012349972"><br/>4.5*<br/><br/><br/>Re-read 20th April 2018<br/><br/>While I originally read this back in 2011 I’ve never actually reviewed it until now.<br/><br/>The first chapter is one I always remember and chapter 3 is where I fully rediscover exactly why I love these books so much.   <span id="freeText16009064115012349972" style="display:none"><br />4.5*<br /><br /><br />Re-read 20th April 2018<br /><br />While I originally read this back in 2011 I’ve never actually reviewed it until now.<br /><br />The first chapter is one I always remember and chapter 3 is where I fully rediscover exactly why I love these books so much. Ty takes Zane to West Virginia to meet his family and the conversation and easy humour pulled me straight back in.<br />I love Chester and his shovel, Ty’s brother Deuce and the whole Grady clan, although reluctantly at times where Earl is concerned. <br /><br />As always with these guys they can’t catch a break and their easy vacation turns into something else entirely.<br /><br />A shout out to Ty’s T.shirts again.<br /><br />“Schitt Creek Paddle Co”<br /><br />And so it’s straight onto Fish &amp; Chips for me now.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2261486543" />
    <a title="Literatures Movies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66216992-literatures-movies"><img alt="Literatures Movies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522073764p2/66216992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2261486543?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literatures Movies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literatures Movies" href="/user/show/66216992-literatures-movies">Literatures Movies</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2261486543" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17418064719597202198">My, my, my.<br/><br/>I think I might have liked this one a teeny, tiny bit more than the first book. I guess it is true what everyone says, it does gets better and better. <br/><br/>I love Zane and Ty. <br/><br/>I want more Ty and Zane. <br/><br/>There will never be enough of these two.<br/><br/> You can quite literally write a whole book of them just sitting around doing nothing and I would still read it. I have caught onto the Zane and Ty fever y'all. And I ain't regretting nothing. The only thing I regret is that I didn't caught onto this tr</span>
  <span id="freeText17418064719597202198" style="display:none">My, my, my.<br><br>I think I might have liked this one a teeny, tiny bit more than the first book. I guess it is true what everyone says, it does gets better and better. <br><br>I love Zane and Ty. <br><br>I want more Ty and Zane. <br><br>There will never be enough of these two.<br><br> You can quite literally write a whole book of them just sitting around doing nothing and I would still read it. I have caught onto the Zane and Ty fever y'all. And I ain't regretting nothing. The only thing I regret is that I didn't caught onto this train sooner <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521515178ra/25241981.gif" width="450" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521515178ra/25241982.gif" width="450" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*wink*<br><br>Anyways. While I enjoyed this book, it feels like nothing is really going on in this one. I'm not complaining. It's nice to be able to get to know Ty's family and see Ty and Zane's relationship grow, but at the same time, it kinda feels as if a lot of things are going on all at once, but then again, it feels as if nothing is really actually progressing. I don't know. This book kinda feel more like an intermezzo, like a novella, rather than a full novel if you get what I mean<br><br>I love Ty's family, all but that one motherfucker <i> Earl </i>. That man is so annoying sometimes I feel like I want to go into the book and strangle him myself. There are all kinds of love in the world, and <i>Earl</i> is supposedly the definition of #toughlove. But man, that ain't no tough love. He's the epitome of that one dumb character in the book who has too much pride, yet not enough brain to back it up and the only reason he has the sway that he did was because he was a senior. <br><br>Like no. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1474463674ra/20603130.gif" width="450" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Things don't work like that, <i> Earl </i>. Not to mention, this man went around and apologize to quite literally everyone but Ty. Like bitch? Ty was the one who was truly hurt from what <i>Earl's</i> dumbass self said and yet <i>Earl</i> could not swallow down his big-ass pride to apologize face to face?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521515178ra/25241983.gif" width="450" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Shoo satan. Get away from my precious babies. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521515178ra/25241984.gif" width="450" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Other than that, I have no complaints. As a lot of you know by now, I'm pretty much trash for Ty and Zane. So I mean<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520592115ra/25185814.gif" width="450" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Please bear with my fangirling self for a little bit longer? <br><br><br><br><b> Blog: <a href="http://literaturesandmovies.com" rel="nofollow noopener">I write reviews on my blog too! :D </a></b></span>

  <i>Cut &amp; Run</i>
</b> series and if you have already read the first book there is no way you can go past this one.<br><br>I have already my favorite M/M-Genre-guys. But <b>Zane</b> and <b>Ty</b> are almost as good as my <b>Vadim</b> and <b>Dan</b>. <br><b>
  <u>It is impossible NOT to fall in love with them!</u>
</b><br><br>They are a <b>perfect team</b>, the <b>perfect partners</b> for each other, they are without any hesitation one of the best if not <b>the best mm-couple</b>, and the second book in the series was a best proof for it. <br><br>Three-week vacation for <b>Zane</b> and <b>Ty</b>! <br>Hiking in West Virginia! <div id="review_3500172575" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3500172575" />
    <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse"><img alt="Ms. Smartarse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401273675p2/13703358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3500172575?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=mm">mm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=action-adventure">action-adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=friendship">friendship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=survival">survival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=part_of_a_series">part_of_a_series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3500172575" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3472786079341908279">Ty and Zane have been relegated to desk duty for the past six months, and they're seriously chafing at their restraints. Unsurprisingly, this shows in their psych evals, especially Zane's. So their boss very kindly forces them to go on vacation to Ty's home town. An excellent opportunity for Zane to see that Ty's craziness runs in the family. For maximum impression, a bit of dangerous hiking is added, with a generous serving of therapeutic chatting courtesy of Ty's psychiatrist brother. Just a b</span>
  <span id="freeText3472786079341908279" style="display:none">Ty and Zane have been relegated to desk duty for the past six months, and they're seriously chafing at their restraints. Unsurprisingly, this shows in their psych evals, especially Zane's. So their boss very kindly forces them to go on vacation to Ty's home town. An excellent opportunity for Zane to see that Ty's craziness runs in the family. For maximum impression, a bit of dangerous hiking is added, with a generous serving of therapeutic chatting courtesy of Ty's psychiatrist brother. Just a bit of Grady family hospitality.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599158030ra/30057449.gif" alt="babbling brook" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story itself didn't impress me too much. There's a lot of hiking, hiding their relationship from the parents (the brother has a 6th sense), and getting pissed off at Ty's authoritarian father. A far cry from the action-packed investigating of the prequel, but we can't have it all. <br><br>On the plus side, there's a ton of character development to be had, along with some important changes in Ty and Zane's relationship, even with their relatively sparse interaction. Plus Ty's family's idiosyncrasies are hell'a funny. In a, you know, these people are should be certified kind of way.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1599158557ra/30057507.gif" alt="To the shovel" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
<br>"It's not <em>that</em> weird. I sleep with a gun," Zane said with a shrug, though he was bemused. "You used to sleep with any number of weapons. Why not a shovel?" He paused and bit his lip. "What kind of damage can he do with that thing?"<br>"Broke my nose when I was fifteen," Ty answered with a fond smile. ""He can hit a snake from ten yards away. Moving target's iffy since his eyesight started going," he added seriously.<br>
</blockquote><br><br><strong>Score: 3/5 stars</strong><br><br>Not quite at binging level, but there's noticeable improvement in the writing and the character development fronts. Also, Deuce is brilliant and should feature more prominently in future books. <br>All in all: the series shows definite promise.<br><br>=======================<br>Review of book 1: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3500167752" rel="nofollow noopener">Cut &amp; Run</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2639679643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18326318922397540355">It looks like Ty and Zane are one of those couples that attract danger anywhere they go, and they manage to save the day! My favorite kind of couple. When the book started with vacation I wondered to myself:"What could possibly happen in the woods?" Well, boys did sure have themselves a VACATION!!! <br/><br/>But first, I want to say how much I loved the Grady family, well, most of them. Earl Grady is in the dog house! The gall of the man!!! But Chester Grady! Oh wow, he is one of those family members each</span>
  <span id="freeText18326318922397540355" style="display:none">It looks like Ty and Zane are one of those couples that attract danger anywhere they go, and they manage to save the day! My favorite kind of couple. When the book started with vacation I wondered to myself:"What could possibly happen in the woods?" Well, boys did sure have themselves a VACATION!!! <br /><br />But first, I want to say how much I loved the Grady family, well, most of them. Earl Grady is in the dog house! The gall of the man!!! But Chester Grady! Oh wow, he is one of those family members each family must have - he is so funny! I loved Deacon and Mara too! I hope they will feature in the coming books more. <br /><br />The danger that the boys find themselves in this time is not official, it takes a lot of courage and lack of common sense to get out of this pickle. There were moments when I doubted they even could get out. But never have I doubted that something serious and lasting was developing between Ty and Zane. Even in danger and hurt they still looked out for each other, even seeing each other at their worst it could not stop them from trusting and leaning on each other even more than before.<br /><br />I loved the last chapter. Ty was so shy and endearing. *sigh* And Zane it seemed was in the right place to start putting himself back together to be the man he was always supposed to be. I am so looking forward to their adventures! I highly recommend it! </span>
  <a data-text-id="18326318922397540355" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2635054255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1124094941647382452">If you're a fan of m/m romantic thrillers, then you can't beat the writing pair of Urban and Roux for incredible fiction, and in Sticks & Stones, the sequel to one of my favorite reads of 2009, Cut & Run, the irresistible and at times irascible FBI Special Agents Zane Garrett and Ty Grady are back with a vengeance. They're still toting around all sorts of personal and professional baggage and struggling with the aftereffects of a case that nearly killed them both, not to mention struggling with </span>
  <span id="freeText1124094941647382452" style="display:none">If you're a fan of m/m romantic thrillers, then you can't beat the writing pair of Urban and Roux for incredible fiction, and in Sticks &amp; Stones, the sequel to one of my favorite reads of 2009, Cut &amp; Run, the irresistible and at times irascible FBI Special Agents Zane Garrett and Ty Grady are back with a vengeance. They're still toting around all sorts of personal and professional baggage and struggling with the aftereffects of a case that nearly killed them both, not to mention struggling with their relationship with each other, and yet - thanks to incredible writing and exquisitely detailed characterization - this second book drives home just how amazing a read can be when you transcend the idea of character and plot and start to experience in a profound way these two men's lives.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1124094941647382452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

End of review.<br/><br/><b>Reread in March, 2020:</b> And yes, I still love this book and think it's pretty goddamn epic. //<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Osm++fV92yDiSJX518TdTSu2mHXO5yyHwKv+gBdRMpoBtaBUjHwT8tKaQnv5Ssey6YFwx0KvTDfO6hKxWtbfbg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iCVjAa7X+DMXxPofE3trpRAecd683Qf1lB+oNmxT5myzWX2s19Yw4ScWLZ099XFa0imZbDCVZ0WaXkQHIdQLmA==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17975766750468227364">Abigail Roux was born and raised in North Carolina. A past volleyball star who specializes in sarcasm and painful historical accuracy, she currently spends her time coaching high school volleyball and investigating the mysteries of single motherhood. Any spare time is spent living and dying with every Atlanta Braves and Carolina Panthers game of the year. Abigail has a daughter, Little Roux, who i</span>
  <span id="freeText17975766750468227364" style="display:none">Abigail Roux was born and raised in North Carolina. A past volleyball star who specializes in sarcasm and painful historical accuracy, she currently spends her time coaching high school volleyball and investigating the mysteries of single motherhood. Any spare time is spent living and dying with every Atlanta Braves and Carolina Panthers game of the year. Abigail has a daughter, Little Roux, who is the light of her life, a boxer, four rescued cats who play an ongoing live-action variation of 'Call of Duty' throughout the house, a certifiable extended family down the road, and a cast of thousands in her head.</span>
